  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a0343be1-0c2e-442d-810e-42cbbf1cd8a5'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText3175237338832512119" style="display:none">***This novel contains graphic sexual content and harsh language. It is only appropriate for adult readers age 18+. <br /><br />Have you ever been so angry that hitting things felt good? Or so numb that you actually felt high? The past few years have been like that for me. Traveling between fury and indifference with no stops in between.<br /><br />Some people hate me for it, while others are scared of me. But none of them can hurt me, because I don't care about anything or anyone.<br /><br />Except Tatum.<br /><br />I love her so much that I hate her. We used to be friends, but I found out that I couldn't trust her or anyone else.<br /><br />So I hurt her. I pushed her away.<br /><br />But I still need her. The sight of her centers me, and I can pool all of my anger into her. Engaging her, challenging her, bullying her...they are my food, my air, and the last part of me that feels anything human.<br /><br />But she left. She went to France for a year, and came back a different girl.<br /><br />Now, when I push, she pushes back.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer802170587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16193420054722089376"><b>4 Amazingly Written Stars!!!</b><br/><br/>I'll be honest, after reading this book, <b>I STILL DO NOT LIKE JARED</b>–hence the only reason I didn't give this book 5 stars–and, frankly, I continue to struggle to understand <b>WHY</b> Tate would want to take him back after the way he <b>BULLIED</b> her for years. <b>However, that doesn't negate the fact that this is by far the best his-side-of-the-story I've read to date!</b> Holy cow! Penelope Douglas did an amazing job writing Jared's story. I still don't like him but I understand him, a</span>
  <span id="freeText16193420054722089376" style="display:none"><b>4 Amazingly Written Stars!!!</b><br /><br />I'll be honest, after reading this book, <b>I STILL DO NOT LIKE JARED</b>–hence the only reason I didn't give this book 5 stars–and, frankly, I continue to struggle to understand <b>WHY</b> Tate would want to take him back after the way he <b>BULLIED</b> her for years. <b>However, that doesn't negate the fact that this is by far the best his-side-of-the-story I've read to date!</b> Holy cow! Penelope Douglas did an amazing job writing Jared's story. I still don't like him but I understand him, and wasn't that the whole purpose of this book? <br /><br /><i>Until You</i> is not just the retelling of <i>Bully</i> from Jared's POV. <i>Until You</i> is fresh, unique, and definitely its own story. It helps readers understand Jared and why he behaved the way he did. It doesn't excuse his actions but gives a better understanding of what motivated them. <br /><br />Bravo to you Ms. Douglas. You accomplishing what few authors have...writing a superbly written his-side-of-the-story book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16193420054722089376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680887701?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18260742-until-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680887701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7515400381292846036"><br/><br/><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/5a953281-083c-4cc9-a831-43a52eb3effa_zps0bfacfae.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586446.jpg' alt=' photo 5a953281-083c-4cc9-a831-43a52eb3effa_zps0bfacfae.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Sometimes, I have issues with 1.5 books that are essentially the first book from a different p.o.v. Luckily, this book wasn’t like that. It didn’t feel like Bully from another perspective. You still got the ‘Bully’ story, but there was a lot of new scenes and new information. <br/><br/><b>Jared</b><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/6bddb81d-c4c6-4792-b976-a2943e662df9_zps9901ae20.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586447.jpg' alt=' photo 6bddb81d-c4c6-4792-b976-a2943e662df9_zps9901ae20.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/> Jared is a bully. He knows it. He’s a bully to one particular person. Tate. Tate was Jared’s best friend for a long time. Then one summer, he went to stay with his father. When he came back, everything</span>
  <span id="freeText7515400381292846036" style="display:none"><br><br><b>5 Stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/5a953281-083c-4cc9-a831-43a52eb3effa_zps0bfacfae.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586446.jpg" alt=" photo 5a953281-083c-4cc9-a831-43a52eb3effa_zps0bfacfae.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sometimes, I have issues with 1.5 books that are essentially the first book from a different p.o.v. Luckily, this book wasn’t like that. It didn’t feel like Bully from another perspective. You still got the ‘Bully’ story, but there was a lot of new scenes and new information. <br><br><b>Jared</b><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/6bddb81d-c4c6-4792-b976-a2943e662df9_zps9901ae20.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586447.jpg" alt=" photo 6bddb81d-c4c6-4792-b976-a2943e662df9_zps9901ae20.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> Jared is a bully. He knows it. He’s a bully to one particular person. Tate. Tate was Jared’s best friend for a long time. Then one summer, he went to stay with his father. When he came back, everything changed. Jared was a different person. He dealt with things the only way he knew how. By making Tate’s life hell.<br><br>I won’t rehash the entire story. If you’ve read Bully, you know the gist. If you haven’t, check it out (or my review of Bully). Just know that Jared goes through some big changes and revelations. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/f32abd79-e21a-4653-942a-176de9da1e75_zps09f381c3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586448.jpg" alt=" photo f32abd79-e21a-4653-942a-176de9da1e75_zps09f381c3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Seeing Jared grow and evolve as a person was a wonderful thing. I loved watching Tate and Jared become friends again, and continue to move forward. Jared has always had feelings for Tate. Even longer than we knew. It was so nice to see inside of his head. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/40c624c0-f6c6-4ef2-9fd3-0944eefd2287_zps33270ef0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586449.jpg" alt=" photo 40c624c0-f6c6-4ef2-9fd3-0944eefd2287_zps33270ef0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Books are always better from the male point of view. Always. We already knew why Jared was the way he was to an extent. But to know the full reasons, how he felt, it made more sense. I loved Jared in Bully. Even when I thought he was just a straight up asshole, I still loved him. There was just something about him. Now, reading this book, it made me love him even more. Could you read this without first reading Bully? Yes. Would I recommend reading Bully first? Yes. This is a fantastic series you won’t want to miss out on. It’s got so many fantastic characters, I’m happy that it’s continuing. I love Jared’s friend Madoc just as much as I love Jared so I can’t wait for his book next! <br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/7063d425-7c34-4e57-8fc5-9b0601044f67_zps944f3f9d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387378071i/7586450.jpg" alt=" photo 7063d425-7c34-4e57-8fc5-9b0601044f67_zps944f3f9d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_681185440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681185440" />
    <a title="Geri Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads"><img alt="Geri Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487874758p2/11757728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681185440?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geri Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geri Reads" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18260742-until-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681185440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3863240651248507162"><b>5 never-a-dull-moment stars!! This book was one heck of a ride. Being in Jared's head was at times scary, frustrating, sad, dirty--like really dirty--but still effin' enjoyable. Not to mention this book is HOT! Like really panty-melting and so raunchy, it should be illegal, kind of hot.</b><br/><br/>First off, I have to congratulate Penelope Douglas for truly giving us Jared's story. This book wasn't a rehash of Bully. While there are plenty of things here that we've already seen/read from Bully, we also get </span>
  <span id="freeText3863240651248507162" style="display:none"><b>5 never-a-dull-moment stars!! This book was one heck of a ride. Being in Jared's head was at times scary, frustrating, sad, dirty--like really dirty--but still effin' enjoyable. Not to mention this book is HOT! Like really panty-melting and so raunchy, it should be illegal, kind of hot.</b><br><br>First off, I have to congratulate Penelope Douglas for truly giving us Jared's story. This book wasn't a rehash of Bully. While there are plenty of things here that we've already seen/read from Bully, we also get a lot, and I mean, A LOT of new scenes about Jared, about his father, his relationship with his mother, Jax and Madoc. And we really get to know what he's thinking during those times where he made Tate's life miserable. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2u9qq8h" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386352403i/7345286.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Until You starts off with a 10-year old Jared meeting a 10-year old Tate for the first time. It was very cute and we see a glimpses of their relationship prior to the "Bully" years through Jared's memory. It was through this flashbacks that we found out what pushed Jared to make that life-changing decision to spend his summer with his dad when he was 14 and the falling out with Tate afterwards. <br><br><b>
  <i>And it ain't pretty.</i>
</b><br><br><b>Jared</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/xS3cZQG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382199274i/5748315._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Jared is one angry dude. Really angry. You can feel his anger, his loss of control. He just wants to lash out. The problem is he couldn't lash out at the people who have hurt him and abandoned him, mainly his father and mother. So he focused all his anger at that one person.<br><br><b>
  <i>Tate</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2nkj6g0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386355484i/7346165._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Poor Tate. She took the brunt of Jared's anger without ever really knowing why. All she can do was cry and suffer in silence until she decided to fight back and give Jared the 'middle finger.'<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/v2VrimO" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381230630ra/4566589.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The I-want-you-but-I-hate-you signal coming from Jared drove me batshit crazy at times. But I really can't complain that much since that's one of the best part of this book. Jared tried so hard so hold on to his hate but found himself falling deeper and deeper in love with Tate instead. When he's not being an ass though, Jared can be sweet, funny and protective. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1z87xk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386352403ra/7345287.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But what I like best about this book was that despite showing us Jared's atrocious experience at the hands of his father, it was never used as a vehicle to justify Jared's action. In fact, this book shows how illogical Jared's thought process was when it comes to Tate. So if you read this book searching for more answers as to why, you might be disappointed. But that doesn't mean Jared didn't redeem himself. He did. But he redeemed himself by actually admitting it and not because we get a clear cut explanation on why he bullied Tate.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“There are times when we can blame a situation on others, but we own our reactions to them. There comes a point where we are the ones responsible for our choices and excuses don’t carry weight anymore.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The only thing I didn't like about this book is KC. Yeah. Sorry, but I really didn't buy that making Liam jealous angle. As if she didn't enjoy Jared's attention. *Roll eyes* Okay. So I'm a little jealous of the skank but can you really blame me? <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/t9UuCOK" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380417966ra/827213.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>ARC is provided by the author in exchange for an honest review.</i><br>____________________________________________________________________________<br><b>I just got my ARC!!!Weeeh!! I can't wait to get inside Jared's head!! Yay!! </b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/h2q0Iyo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385895294ra/7253308.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Q3xzukx" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383835801ra/6680428.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>The cover is gorgeous by the way! And if you click on the image below, it will take to Chapter One of Until You. <br><br><a href="http://everafterromancebookblog.blogspot.com/2013/07/cover-reveal-and-teaser-until-you-fall.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431123i/864956._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3863240651248507162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1366471962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366471962" />
    <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance"><img alt="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376622739p2/5498948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1366471962?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance">Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=steamy-romance">steamy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=keeper-shelf">keeper-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=books-i-d-reread-over-over">books-i-d-reread-over-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1366471962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4129660328534385159"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440106102r/15930278.jpg?v=1440106105606' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png' width='50' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Becoming hard at heart isn't an intersection in your brain where you have a choice to turn left or right. It's coming to a dead end, and you just keep going, over the cliff, unable to stop the inevitable, because the truth is you just don't want to.<br/>There is freedom in the fall.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415830267ra/11852600.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>If I'm being perfectly honest, I was actually hesitant to read this. Last time I read a companion novel, the only thing it managed to do was make me hate the heroine with the fire of the worst kind of ve</span>
  <span id="freeText4129660328534385159" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440106102r/15930278.jpg?v=1440106105606" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Becoming hard at heart isn't an intersection in your brain where you have a choice to turn left or right. It's coming to a dead end, and you just keep going, over the cliff, unable to stop the inevitable, because the truth is you just don't want to.<br>There is freedom in the fall.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415830267ra/11852600.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If I'm being perfectly honest, I was actually hesitant to read this. Last time I read a companion novel, the only thing it managed to do was make me hate the heroine with the fire of the worst kind of venereal disease. Not that I'd know what that felt like, but you catch my drift. What I mean to say, is more often then not you're getting the same regurgitated novel you already read but in a different POV. Well this <b>wasn't that at all</b>. Not even a little bit. Not even close. While this is essentially in Jared's POV it's a completely different book. So much so, that you can read it as a standalone, which I wouldn't recommend since you need to see it from Tate's POV first in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20803953.Bully__Fall_Away___1_" title="Bully (Fall Away, #1) by Penelope Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Bully</a>. You may be asking yourself, why wasn't this just written as an alternating POV initially? Well you, my doubtful friend, clearly haven't read the first book, because then you'd understand that no way would it have had the same effect if you got both their POVs in one book. Nope. This story was meant to be told in two books, it two different experiences, by two very different people.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I wanted her to hurt. I didn't want her to hurt.<br>I hated her. I loved her.<br>I wanted to violate her body in a hundred different ways. I wanted to keep her safe.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413862814ra/11574326.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I fell in love with Penelope Douglas's storytelling in Bully, and the only thing this book managed to do was completely reaffirm that. Everything and I mean <i>everything</i> that I wanted more clarification and answers on in Bully was addressed here. While I adored that book, I found the reasons that Jared gave Tate for his behavior in it a little...weak. I felt like it had to be something more, something bigger for him to flip that switch and be the way he was with her. Until You delivered those answers in spades. Penelope truly allows the reader inside Jared's head and you understand him and all his behavior so much more. Plus I loved getting more of him and Madoc and their banter together.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Anyone who sees the way you looks at her knows you don't want to hook up with her. No, right now you're looking at her like you want to tie her up and give her a big, fat spanking."<br>Stupid ass.<br>I wasn't into shit like that, or...I didn't think I was. Never tried it. Might try it, I guess. You should try everything at least once.<br>Except crystal meth.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What I loved the most about Until You was that it was a totally different experience from Bully. You get to see everything from an entirely different perspective. You also get to see that year that Tate was away in France and the spiral that hit Jared. And get to experience all the events that finally lead up to his epiphany about his feelings for her.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Right at that moment, I wanted everything from Tate. Everything. Her anger and passion, her hate and lust, her body and soul.<br>I wanted control of all of it</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440107006r/15930459.jpg?v=1440107010037" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I adored Tate in Bully and I was so happy that didn't change seeing her from Jared's eyes. If anything, it made me like her even more. But what this book managed to do, was endear the reader to Jared completely. The bully that you loved to hate and hated to love in the first book really lets loose his vulnerable side and you appreciate his behavior and the why's of it so much more. It just clicks. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">The hair, the outfit, it was the perfect blend of good girl and bad girl, of salvation and danger.<br>There was no point in lying to myself. As much as I hated her, I wanted a taste of her.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>If you're on the fence about reading this, you need to get the fuck off it! Seriously. The only thing this book will do is make you love Bully even more and fall in love with both these characters even deeper than before.<br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440107201r/15930540.jpg?v=1440107204949" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And this is coming from a reader that has a shorter attention span than a fly. If I get a HEA in one book I'm not typically one to read a second book for them. I call it my book ADD. But this incredible book made me change my view on that completely. I'm so glad I experienced it because it only made me love their story that much more. I'm now a huge fan of this author and can safely say that absolutely anything she'll write, I'll read...without a second thought.<br><br>Read it. Love it. Trust me.<br><br><b>For more reviews visit<br><a href="http://dirtygirlromance.com" target="blogspot" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436477285i/15465455._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4129660328534385159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

That was not the case with this book, it fell apart and got annoyingly cheesy towards the ending. </span>

<div id="review_681239570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681239570" />
    <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog"><img alt="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596881564p2/6603203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681239570?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog">Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

  <span id="freeText7892868101166938956" style="display:none">I've been waiting for Jared's pov!<br>The entire time I was reading Bully I kept wondering what was going on in his head..why did he act like that around Tate and how did he really feel, and that is exactly what we get here!! After reading this, I finally have some closure on what was going through his head. Watching him struggle with his feelings of love for Tate, his feeling of abandonment toward his mother and father were really sad :(( <br>Reading about his thoughts, how his feelings and reasoning it made him so much more lovable!!!<br>Tate was everything to him and deep down he was ashamed for hurting her.<br>I loved reading how much he wanted her. And of course, I loved reading all the intense, hot moments. <span id="freeTextContainer16300869343531845508">Considering I'm generally not a big fan of the "#_.5" companion novels of any series since it's typically the story I just read merely from another POV ... I am shocked, y'all... <b>*SHOCKED*</b> that I'm giving this book a 5 star rating. But, here I am... tacking all 5 stars to this bad boy. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504819485ra/23825624.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Penelope Douglas gave us a unicorn here, folks. One of the few companion books that really friggin' works. I <i>may</i> even like it MORE than I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067567849?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bully</a>. The fantastic thing about this book is that it isn't a case of</span>
  <span id="freeText16300869343531845508" style="display:none">Considering I'm generally not a big fan of the "#_.5" companion novels of any series since it's typically the story I just read merely from another POV ... I am shocked, y'all... <b>*SHOCKED*</b> that I'm giving this book a 5 star rating. But, here I am... tacking all 5 stars to this bad boy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504819485ra/23825624.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Penelope Douglas gave us a unicorn here, folks. One of the few companion books that really friggin' works. I <i>may</i> even like it MORE than I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067567849?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Bully</a>. The fantastic thing about this book is that it isn't a case of simply changing the POV, slapping a new cover on it and calling it a "companion". This story has more.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504819261ra/23825535.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, yes... there's more! And, I will not complain about more Jared. <br>And Tate. <br>But, mostly Jared because as I've stated many times before... I'm a sucker for a complete alphahole.<br><br>Now, yes, of course we're given the same story concept and major dialogue we had in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20803953.Bully__Fall_Away___1_" title="Bully (Fall Away, #1) by Penelope Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Bully</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441375537ra/16101087.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But there are scenes we weren't privy to in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20803953.Bully__Fall_Away___1_" title="Bully (Fall Away, #1) by Penelope Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Bully</a> and way more important info we weren't given before that we do get in this book. Ergo...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504819261ra/23825536.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yep! And, it's fan-fucking-tastic! We also become more acquainted with characters who will most definitely be playing bigger roles in future books. <br><br>Listen, peeps... Penelope Douglas is an absolutely engaging writer. She has without a doubt become a one-click author for me. She gives me all the feels with her writing. ALL. THE. FEELS. I can't wait to dive into more of her yummy good books.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11690516555251847727">*EXCERPT*<br/><br/>Over the years, Tate had endured a lot of harassment because of me. People were pretty stupid in high school and freshman and sophomores are the dumbest. They want to be accepted, and gossip is taken as gospel. Tell people that someone has their clit pierced or that they eat dogs, and you just have to sit back and watch the school flood with talk. And usually the objects of the talk would drown pretty quickly.<br/>However, by junior and senior year, silly rumors are about as effective as a b</span>
  <span id="freeText11690516555251847727" style="display:none">*EXCERPT*<br /><br />Over the years, Tate had endured a lot of harassment because of me. People were pretty stupid in high school and freshman and sophomores are the dumbest. They want to be accepted, and gossip is taken as gospel. Tell people that someone has their clit pierced or that they eat dogs, and you just have to sit back and watch the school flood with talk. And usually the objects of the talk would drown pretty quickly.<br />However, by junior and senior year, silly rumors are about as effective as a broken condom. I’d wanted to keep guys away from Tate, but that wasn’t working so much anymore. They saw she was beautiful, and now, after the locker room incident, they saw her as a slut, too. <br />“Jared’s right. You’re not worth it.” Nate’s voice was low, but I was already on his ass. <br />“Sit down, Nate.”<br />He spun around, while Tate looked up. I didn’t make eye contact with her, but I knew her eyes were on me.<br />Dietrich looked surprised and small. He knew not to mess with me as did most of the school. I wasn’t huge, and I had no special skills that other guys didn’t have, but I wasn’t afraid. Ever. I didn’t mind getting hit, and I didn’t back down.<br />That’s what scared most people about me.<br />You come at me, and I’ll come after you harder. <br />“Hey, man, no offense.” He held up his hands. “If you’re not done with her…”<br />My arms surged with the need to haul this guy out of here by his collar.<br />If I’m not done with her?<br />And just then, I felt like crawling inside of myself to hide.<br />My throat tightened, and my eyes burned.<br />What the hell?<br />I wanted her to hurt, but I didn’t want her to hurt. I hated her. I loved her. I wanted to violate her body in a hundred different ways, but I wanted to keep her safe.<br />There was no limit to how fucking confused I was right now, but one thing was for certain.<br />Tate was worth more than all of us put together.<br />She wasn’t trash.<br />She was hope and sunlight, and all the good shit that assholes like us don’t get.<br />And for the first time, I wasn’t getting any goddamn peace from tormenting this girl. I just wanted to wrap her up in my arms and see her happy. <br />My eyes narrowed, and I wished for a perfect world where I could toss darts at this guy’s dick. “Don’t talk to her again,” I commanded. “Go.” And I jerked my chin off to a corner he should go fucking hide in. <br />Was I better than him?<br />No. But I’d deal with that shit later.<br />Tate let out an aggravated sigh as Nate walked off, and I turned my eyes on her in time to see her lips tighten. I saw the scowl, knew it was meant for me, but didn’t even have a chance to figure out why when she spoke up.<br />“Don’t do me any favors,” she sneered. “You’re a miserable piece of shit, Jared. But then, I guess I’d be miserable, too, if my parents hated me. Your dad left you, and your mom avoids you. But who can blame them, right?” <br />I stopped breathing, and the room around me closed in.<br />What the fuck did she just say?<br />I stared at her, feeling torn apart and dead, knowing that it was completely un-Tate to say something like that but also knowing that she spoke the truth.<br />I didn’t forget to breathe. I just didn’t want to anymore.<br />It felt like every eye in the room was on me and people were whispering behind their hands, laughing at me. I was exposed, and everyone knew my shit.<br />My eyes sharpened on her, and I wasn’t at all confused anymore about whether I loved or hated her.<br />I fucking hated her.<br />She was packaged up to look like a good girl, but make no mistake. There was bitch in there, and thank God I was reminded of that fact.<br /><br /><br />Enter to win giveaways on my blog....<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.anniebrewerwrites.com/2013/08/bully-blog-tour-until-you-by-penelope.html">http://www.anniebrewerwrites.com/2013...</a><br /><br /><br />Edit: HOLY SHIT!!!!! That cover.....seriously I wanna lick it and maybe caress it and rub it on myself....wait, TMI. Sorry. But holy hell, Jared, you are one juicy sexy bad boy and I can't wait to get my hands on you. Excuse me while I run a cold shower cause right now I'm sweating....<br /><br />Woohoo!!!!!! I'm so so so so so so excited for this book!!!!! Or partial book, or whatever! I don't care, I just can't wait to read from Jared's pov!!!!! I was having mixed feelings for him in Bully. But since I'm a bad boy kinda girl, I ended up loving him. Not that his bad boy sexy charm made up for all the shit he did to Tate. But.....yeah, I fell for him anyway. And now we get his POV! So thank you Penelope, I can't wait!!!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15600697439142041171">IT'S OUT GUYS!!! Can I just mention how unbelievably excited I am to read this!?!?!? <i>SQUEEE!!</i><br/><br/>If you guys have already read it, tell me what you think of it :)<br/><br/><b><u>CASTING</u><br/><br/>Jared Trent<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428205i/856611._SY540_.jpg' width='240' height='339' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Tate Holloway<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383348872i/6515918._SY540_.jpg' width='240' height='340' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></b></span>
  <span id="freeText15600697439142041171" style="display:none">IT'S OUT GUYS!!!     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_681196430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681196430" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681196430?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18260742-until-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=zero-stars-is-too-much-for-this">zero-stars-is-too-much-for-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dropped-series">dropped-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681196430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6833720905610901817"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Well, at least I gave this read a shot. I read though the whole thing, but it was goodness awful. But I'm going to talk about it like the read I treated it as - mostly through something of an academic/curious filter.<br/><br/>It was rough going though, and I do not understand the appeal of Jared at all.<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>There's much for me to cover in this review, so I won't mince too many words here in establishing the plot, just get right to my reaction for turns of events. I wasn't going to</span>
  <span id="freeText6833720905610901817" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> Well, at least I gave this read a shot. I read though the whole thing, but it was goodness awful. But I'm going to talk about it like the read I treated it as - mostly through something of an academic/curious filter.<br /><br />It was rough going though, and I do not understand the appeal of Jared at all.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />There's much for me to cover in this review, so I won't mince too many words here in establishing the plot, just get right to my reaction for turns of events. I wasn't going to read this given my reaction to "Bully", but considering this was the "hero" follow-up, I decided to bite the bullet and read this purely as a measure of curious/academic discourse. Meaning I read much of this through an emotional filter on purpose to see if "Until You" made the series any better than its first novel by showcasing its respective hero in the front seat. To reveal a bias upfront, I hated Jared's character in "Bully." Hated him to the finest point and I didn't think of him as a proper love interest in the slightest. I wondered how anyone could romanticize a guy who, despite the notation of his tormented past with abuse and neglect, had such an abrasive, control freak personality. I suppose I got my answer in this book with a more intimate perspective of Jared's viewpoint and experiences, but I can't say I'm happy with it at all. <br /><br />If anything, "Until You" is worse in quality than "Bully." "Bully," to its credit was compulsively readable in places, and Tate's perspective made some turns of it tolerable. This read slow, tedious, and didn't have a sympathetic eye to Jared's perspective point really at all. He's pretty much a possessive, violent control freak with moments of nearly raping Tatum, but yet has the gall to not equate himself with "assholes" who harrass women.<br /><br />Oh, the ever-loving irony.<br /><br />Being in Jared's head felt like a poison that I couldn't get out fast enough from. He's worse than Travis Maddox in my opinion. I hate saying that because pretty much in the scheme of New Adult, Travis Maddox (hero from Jamie McGuire's "Beautiful" series) is the template go-to guy for abusive alpha males who are violent, misogynstic jerks who have messed up pasts supposedly. (Only, to be blunt, Travis really doesn't have such a messed up past - he lost his mom and then basically has this abrasive personality all on his own, so...)<br /><br />Those of you who've read "Bully" already know much of this story at least for Tate's perspective. It's the same script, different cast for the most part, and while I noted the author made the note that this is "Jared's story" and not a retelling - I hate to say it, but this really is a retelling in so many words. It has a lot of new scenes from Jared's perspective point that provide expansions where the first novel did not on his respective character, much much of it is the cross-between points of events that happened in the first novel. It's not a complete copy/pasta, but much of it is retreaded territory. "Until You" is guilty of doing the exact same thing as "Walking Disaster," "Losing Hope," and pretty much any New Adult popular retelling where the hero's in the front seat.<br /><br />The difference with this novel is that it's not so intricately entwined to the first that you'd miss something if you haven't read the first one. Which, to Douglas's credit, I was able to remember key events in the narrative at the prompting without necessarily going back to the first. But Jared is not as compelling a narrator as Tatum and this read incredibly slow and extremely shallow for emotional quality. There's really very little holding the fabric of this novel together in terms of portraying a sympathetic hero to root for because Jared uses Tate (and pretty much everyone else he knows) like a drug, like a toy to be possessed. He wants to own every part of Tate's life - her fear, her frustration, her anxiety. And even when he starts to see that what he's done to her in terms of her breaking point, it's not a transition that feels all that realistic, just convenient to get the machine in place for their love connections to start.<br /><br />Jared is a human leech, and he makes no qualms about it in the beginning of this novel (well past the first couple of chapters which establish how Tate and Jared met as kids, but that felt incredibly loose in establishment.) Much of the information on his past is communicated in telling form, not showing, and there were points where I wanted to be in his head for proper character development, but didn't see that. There were others I honestly wanted out of his head because of his controlling, violent demeanor - it was too much and hard to see any sympathetic qualities at all. One of the times when Tatum was being bullied by a group over insults towards her body, on one hand he didn't support that because he loved her body (and continuously reminded the reader of that in distinct objectifications), but he was perfectly willing to let Tate believe what she wanted in terms of his thoughts on the matter, making her hurt worse and gaining gratification from that.<br /><br />How is this a romantic hero by any measure of the word? Why do people like reading about characters like this? I do not understand it at all. Granted, I can read about problematic characters - there are some very well written problematic characters out there who redeem themselves to great people by the end of the story. But that's not this story at all. This is a pretty shallow narrative that's championing Jared's worse qualities as romanticized, and that's not cool. It's only by the sake of convenience that Jared's portrayed in any kind of redemptive light here. There are points here where he recognizes his wrongs, but it's much like "Walking Disaster" with the portrayal - he feels guilty for the moment, and then the next he's like "Mine, Mine, Mine!" for using whomever he can, whenever he can.<br /><br />There's a lot of new information shed on Jared's relationship with K.C. in this book, which was ultimately revealed to be a ploy by K.C. to make her old boyfriend jealous. What made it worse was that Jared was perfectly willing to go along with this plan, to use K.C. for her plan and also use K.C. to hurt Tate, to control Tate's emotions and possess her. He didn't want her to belong to anyone. It was so frustrating to read and hard to see how any one this messed up could be worth following in any measure of the word.<br /><br />There's also information about Jared's little brother Jax and Jared's mother that weren't in "Bully", and that provided some relief, but Jax is pretty much the pawn in the manipulative games that Jared's father - from prison, plays with him. And as for Jared's mother (his poor mother) - Jared disrespects and disregards her every chance he can get.<br /><br />There's not much more to say about Tatum here than is mostly known from "Bully" - and you get more of a vantage point difference with Jared being on the outside looking into her life. It made me appreciate more , despite Tatum's respective flaws, that she was the better person to follow and that Jared's POV was never needed in the first place.<br /><br />I don't think this book did much more than confirm that Jared was a worse hero than I believed possible with his respective musings and actions. The set up might have you believe that he's worth redemption because of his so called "tragic past", but while that's explored to a degree, it doesn't make any of his actions justifiable, any of his thoughts have merit, nor are there really very many moments of true redemption here, just championing of flaws that are violent, controlling and really downright offensive to the point of blatant glorification. And yes, the scene where he's forcing himself on Tatum and she pushes against him and tells him to stop comes across as "rapey." It's just as terrible as it was in the first book, only his thoughts make it moreso.<br /><br />Suffice to say, this is my last following of the series, because I can't say that I want to follow any of the other characters from this series further, even of Madoc gets his own story. I imagine that won't turn out much better either given his portrayal here. =/<br /><br />Overall score: 0/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="6833720905610901817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622498901" />
    <a title="Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde"><img alt="Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587623616p2/17243568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622498901?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)*" href="/user/show/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde">Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=for-science">for-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=all-for-love">all-for-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=friskie-mittens-in-public">friskie-mittens-in-public</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622498901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer63878155853313530"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461798423ra/18912940.gif' width='499' height='281' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4 beautiful-mess Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462233467i/18969518._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>While I appreciate the sentiment of the above statement, I also <i>know</i> it to be complete garbage, sometimes. It <b>can</b> cost, a whole hell of a lot, to be kind. Cruelty can be far easier than kindness, especially when it is what has left the most impact on your life. I’m certainly not saying it’s the wise course, but it is a slippery slope that is A LOT easier to fall down than it’s made to seem. <br/><br/>In no way am I condoning Jarod’s behaviour by these remarks. What he did was deplor</span>
  <span id="freeText63878155853313530" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461798423ra/18912940.gif" width="499" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4 beautiful-mess Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462233467i/18969518._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>While I appreciate the sentiment of the above statement, I also <i>know</i> it to be complete garbage, sometimes. It <b>can</b> cost, a whole hell of a lot, to be kind. Cruelty can be far easier than kindness, especially when it is what has left the most impact on your life. I’m certainly not saying it’s the wise course, but it is a slippery slope that is A LOT easier to fall down than it’s made to seem. <br><br>In no way am I condoning Jarod’s behaviour by these remarks. What he did was deplorable! However, under the microscope of the written word and the history of his character, it is <i>understandable</i>. And that is the scary thing about this book for me, probably for a lot of people actually. I am NOT comfortable sympathizing with him as a character. <br><br>I was tormented pretty badly during school; I was chased with knives, teased to the point of tears, bitten, clawed and asked out by a boy on a bet. My school years are not the times I look back on and reminisce. I look back on them as something I <i>survived</i>. It would be dishonest of me to say that I never lashed out at others for being tormented, I did. However, I caught myself on that edge and fought my way back to the kind of person I wanted to be. A kind one. Because while I disagree that it doesn’t cost anything to be kind, I DO agree that it is the stronger choice. To face down cruelty with kindness as my only weapon is one of the most foolish endeavours I have ever taken, however, in choosing that I also chose to not allow others to dictate who I would be. I stand by my choice. <br><br>Jarod went the other route, and I can’t really blame him for that. Being bullied at home is AWFUL! Lashing out is such a viable choice, and lashing out at those you love is even more likely. <br><br>I’m surprised to say that I liked Jarod’s POV in <u>Until You</u> more than I liked Tate’s in <u>Bully</u>. While they take place over the same time frame, for the most part, I found the insight into Jarod’s behaviour both beautiful and disastrous. I’m still curious about the redemption questions I asked when reviewing <u>Bully</u>… however I like the story itself. Even if I find the romantic element rather unbelievable. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462233468ra/18969519.gif" width="500" height="237" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="63878155853313530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14403101709261700145"><b>I LOVED THIS BOOK!</b> I needed Jared' s perspective after reading <i>Bully</i> and I'm so glad Penelope Douglas took the time to write it. I was still a little reluctant to give Jared a free pass on being an asshole douche to Tate for YEARS, but that last scene warmed my cold heart. I can't wait to read Madoc and Jax' s stories.</span>

Until You definitely did its job correctly. My heart ached for Jared in this one, I truly felt for him and, tho I still wanted to sh</span>
  <span id="freeText4930284605982934834" style="display:none">✰ <b>5 stars</b> ✰<br /><br /><b>"My heart only beat for her, and I’d rather spend my life hating, loving, fucking and breathing her than losing her."</b><br /><br /><i>so</i>....there’s a chance I may be whipped for this likable asshole named Jared Trent. 👉🏼👈🏼 I enjoyed Bully, but I had some problems with it - one of them being I needed the H’s pov to understand his perspective and why he was the way he was. Until You definitely did its job correctly. My heart ached for Jared in this one, I truly felt for him and, tho I still wanted to shake him at times for the things he did to Tate, I understood where he was coming from. yes, Jared was the definition of an asshole but was he redeemable? I would have been conflicted with my answer for Bully but in here?? I’d say he redeemed himself in my eyes and his grovelling was much better imo. &lt;33<br /><br />also I kinda know what goes down in Jax/KC’s story but, after their little interactions here, I’m honestly curious enough to wanna read their book. 👀</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12761956546900347293">FYI, yes, my reading progress was <u>very</u> bumpy but after thinking about this book for a while I think the painful journey is worth enduring to get the end story :)<br/><br/><b>4 second-chance stars!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277738._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Words are powerful things. They have the ability to hurt, to heal, to make us feel. Perhaps the only two things stronger than words are music and pictures, which is what this review consists of. <br/><br/><b>It all began with a tree...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277739.jpg' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>And ended with a love story.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277740._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But the in-between? <br/><br/>Well, that’s the <u>best part</u>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277741._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“I’d spent the </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText12761956546900347293" style="display:none">FYI, yes, my reading progress was <u>very</u> bumpy but after thinking about this book for a while I think the painful journey is worth enduring to get the end story :)<br><br><b>4 second-chance stars!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277738._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Words are powerful things. They have the ability to hurt, to heal, to make us feel. Perhaps the only two things stronger than words are music and pictures, which is what this review consists of. <br><br><b>It all began with a tree...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277739.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And ended with a love story.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277740._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the in-between? <br><br>Well, that’s the <u>best part</u>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277741._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“I’d spent the past two years of high school making her life miserable. Telling a few lies, ruining a few dates, all for my own pleasure. Challenging Tate – making her a high school outcast – made my world go round, but she never fought back. Not until now.”</i>
</b> - Jared<br><br><u>Jared</u> is a complex character. The first book only gave us little bits and pieces of Jared’s past, his motives, and his mindset. <i>So many questions.</i><br><br>What really happened that summer? <br>What drove him to turn on Tate? <br>What made him into a <b>
  <i>bully</i>
</b>? <br><br><i>So many faces.</i> <br><br>He’s sexy.<br>He’s <b>tortured</b>.<br>He’s conflicted.<br>He’s <b>broken</b>.<br>He’s protective.<br>He’s <b>
  <i>destructive</i>
</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386033831ra/7277742.gif" width="350" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Tatum?”<br><br>“I wouldn’t care if you were alive or dead.”</i>
</b> - Jared<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277743._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Do you know what this is? It’s me, wiping away the last tear you’ll ever get.”</i>
</b> - Tate<br><br><u>Tate</u> comes back from France with a renewed sense of purpose. She’s ready to put her past behind her, and won’t go down without a fight. <br><br>She’s <b>braver</b>.<br>She’s <b>wiser</b>.<br>She’s <b>
  <i>stronger</i>
</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277744.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jared and Tate are each other’s nemesis and rock. Yin and yang. Drawn towards each other like a moth to a flame. <br><br><b>
  <i>“When you’ve tasted the one thing that fills you up, it’s impossible not to want more of it. A lot more.”</i>
</b> - Jared<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277745._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sticks and stones may break my bones, and words <b>
  <i>will</i>
</b> hurt me. Hurt Tate. Words leave emotional scars that may fade, but never truly go away. In my mind, I could never fully forgive Jared for his past actions, but he sure did one good hell of a job making it up to Tate. And that’s what counts in the end. <br><br>To let love in.<br>To let love stay.<br>To let love heal. <br><br>And let the past <b>
  <i>go</i>
</b>. <br><br><b>
  <i>“You own me body and soul, and everyone is going to know it. Sometimes I’m going to go slow with you, and sometimes I’m going to fuck you. But it will always be love, Tate."</i>
</b> - Jared<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386033831i/7277746.jpg" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>-Lyrics and song from "Skyscraper" by Demi Lovato <br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by author in exchange for an honest review. Please note that all quotes are from an advanced copy and may be subject to change in the final edition.</i> <br></span>

  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br/><br/>I wanted her to hurt. I didn't want her to hurt. I hated her. I loved her...<br/><br/>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg' width='405' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387846598ra/7680682.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I heard we would be getting Jared't POV... And even though by the end of <i>Bully</i> I softened to him slightly, I couldn't love him.</span>
  <span id="freeText8880237157481996631" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380414139i/816192._SX540_.jpg" width="125" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>♥♥♥ 5 Awesome Stars ♥♥♥</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387842007i/7677564._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>I wanted her to hurt. I didn't want her to hurt. I hated her. I loved her...<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387846598ra/7680682.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I heard we would be getting Jared't POV... I could not wait! Why? Well, because, I really liked the book <i>Bully</i>, but had a hard time understanding Jared. I didn't get why he did the things he did to Tate. And even though by the end of <i>Bully</i> I softened to him slightly, I couldn't love him. So, I hoped this book would change my mind... and it totally did.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"I want to touch you," I whispered against her lips. "I want to feel what's mine. What's always been mine."<br><br><i>Please.</i><br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>What I loved about this was that we got a new story. Yes, there were still quite a few of the same scenes, but how can it not? I LOVED the fact that I got so much more new stuff. You get insight in Jared's past, and that terrible summer that changed him. My heart hurt deeply for him. The things he and his younger brother went through in the hands of his father was horrible. I'm actually kind of glad he didn't end up being a lot worse than he was. Still, I didn't agree with his actions.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387847121ra/7680714.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>Tate. My Tate. My best friend, and my worst enemy. The girl that turned my world upside down with her overalls and red baseball cap.<br><br>The only person in every one of my good memories.<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>Tate, I still very much loved. Seeing her in Jared's eyes made me like her more. She was really strong, something I really liked about her. There were so many times where Jared frustrated the crap out of me, though. His way of thinking made no sense at times. He jumped to conclusions too much, just like Tate had as well. His reasons for hurting her were still not right to me. But, I did get him more. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"I can't change the past, Tate. I wish I could, because I'd go back and relive every day that I existed without you, and I'd make sure that you smiled. Every minute of my future belongs to you."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>He may have been a bit of a crazy alpha, and mean at times, but the fact that he admitted it and wanted to be better, is what made me love him. He wasn't perfect, he made so many mistakes. But he wanted to deserve Tate and make everything up to her. He loved her so much, is was the one thing that he was unable to control, but he soon embraced it. He could be really sweet at times, thoughtful, and very dirty minded (which I didn't mind one bit). The steam in this book was higher because of it. I felt like he grew and changed for the better by the end of the book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387846598ra/7680683.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved and was so happy for them because they are on their road to having that friendship back. And also, for them to move forward from all the pain and hurt. I really enjoyed this story so much more, now that I got Jared's POV. I am excited and can't wait to find out what else there is in store for these characters. I can't wait to see how much more they can grow. If you enjoyed <i>Bully</i>, then this is book you must read. You get so much more in this book. It was not a retelling of the same story with the same scenes. It was really well done. Now, I can't wait to read Madoc's book!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794785i/596848._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8880237157481996631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3507817602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3507817602" />
    <a title="manpreet " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32573951-manpreet"><img alt="manpreet " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595523100p2/32573951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3507817602?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="manpreet " class="user" itemprop="url" name="manpreet " href="/user/show/32573951-manpreet">manpreet </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32573951-manpreet?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3507817602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7194179170996201680"><u>4.5 stars!!</u>⛈<br/><br/><i>Until You</i> is the companion novel to the first book in the Fall Away series, <i>Bully</i>. I loved this book so much! After reading <i>Bully</i>, I knew that I needed Jared’s perspective on the situation. And that’s exactly what we got! <br/><br/>I will say, this was my first time reading a companion novel, since I do tend to avoid them for whatever reason. However, after reading the first book, I knew I couldn’t resist - so I was in for a little surprise. I expected this book to just be everything from the </span>
  <span id="freeText7194179170996201680" style="display:none"><u>4.5 stars!!</u>⛈<br /><br /><i>Until You</i> is the companion novel to the first book in the Fall Away series, <i>Bully</i>. I loved this book so much! After reading <i>Bully</i>, I knew that I needed Jared’s perspective on the situation. And that’s exactly what we got! <br /><br />I will say, this was my first time reading a companion novel, since I do tend to avoid them for whatever reason. However, after reading the first book, I knew I couldn’t resist - so I was in for a little surprise. I expected this book to just be everything from the first, just from Jared’s side of the story. And if that was the case, I would still have been happy with the book. BUT, this book was so much more!! A lot of scenes were added that weren’t in the first. Although the major dialogue is exactly the same, there is sO much more background info that the reader didn’t know about. Now I can finally say that I got the closure I needed! <br /><br />Okay since the overall plot is the same as the first, I’ll sum it up quick. Jared and Tate were childhood besties. One summer, Jared goes to visit his father who he hasn’t seen in many years. He had a really bad experience there, and came back a totally changed person. He wanted nothing to do with Tate, and made sure to make her high school years a living hell. <br /><br />Now it’s junior year, and Tate’s studying abroad in France. Jared goes absolutely crazy since he has no one to really target anymore. But when Tate comes back for senior year, she doesn’t just go with the hate, she fights back. <br /><br /><b>“Goddamn.<br />I had no idea what the hell I was going to do now, but one thing was for damn certain.<br />We weren’t done.”</b><br /><br />Just like most enemies to lovers, in the midst of the chaos they find their way back. Not only are they able to gradually build up their friendship to how it was, they go beyond that! <br /><br /><b>“I love you more than myself,” I told her, “more than my own family, for Christ’s sake. I don’t want to take another step in this world without you next to me.”</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and if enemies to lovers is your thing, then do try this out! Not to mention that it is not difficult to fall head over heels for the characters. I look forward to reading the second novel in the series next, that will have more of an emphasis on some side characters! x</span>
